<div id="review_2247408749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2247408749" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2247408749?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062678416" href="/book/show/34848682-the-woman-in-the-window">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2247408749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6255329421988162798">I'm between 3.5 and 4 stars.<br/><br/><i>Paranoia, the destroyer<br/>Self-destroyer, wreck your health<br/>Destroy friends, destroy yourself<br/>The time device of self-destruction<br/>Light the fuse and start eruption</i><br/>—The Kinks, <b>
  <i>Destroyer</i>
</b><br/><br/>Reading A.J. Finn's new, much-hyped thriller, <b>
  <i>The Woman in the Window</i>
</b>, I had lots of paranoia-related songs running through my head (including Garbage's <b>
  <i>I Think I'm Paranoid</i>
</b> and the line from Harvey Danger's <b>
  <i>Flagpole Sitta</i>
</b> which goes, "Paranoia, paranoia, everybody's coming to </span>
  <span id="freeText6255329421988162798" style="display:none">I'm between 3.5 and 4 stars.<br /><br /><i>Paranoia, the destroyer<br />Self-destroyer, wreck your health<br />Destroy friends, destroy yourself<br />The time device of self-destruction<br />Light the fuse and start eruption</i><br />—The Kinks, <b>
  <i>Destroyer</i>
</b><br /><br />Reading A.J. Finn's new, much-hyped thriller, <b>
  <i>The Woman in the Window</i>
</b>, I had lots of paranoia-related songs running through my head (including Garbage's <b>
  <i>I Think I'm Paranoid</i>
</b> and the line from Harvey Danger's <b>
  <i>Flagpole Sitta</i>
</b> which goes, "Paranoia, paranoia, everybody's coming to get me..."), but I felt the above lyrics by The Kinks described this book's protagonist perfectly.<br /><br />Anna Fox used to be a successful child psychologist. She used to have her life together—marriage, family, career—but 11 months ago, a trauma left her with agoraphobia, so she's been unable to step outside of her New York City home all this time. She spends her days watching black and white movies, playing chess and learning French online, drinking too much while ignoring or doubling up on her meds, and counseling others like her in an online forum for people with agoraphobia.<br /><br />She also has a bit of a photography habit, which stems mostly from her interest in watching what is going on outside her home, particularly in the homes of her neighbors. She's seen some pretty interesting things, including the recent afternoon activities of Mrs. Miller, who moved in across the street with her husband.<br /><br />"Watching is like nature photography: You don't interfere with the wildlife."<br /><br />When a new family, the Russells, move in directly across the park from her, Anna is quickly transfixed by them. They seem almost perfect—husband, wife, teenage son. She meets the son first and then the wife, and is amazed at how much she enjoys the wife's company. And then one night, as she watches through their windows, Anna sees something her eyes cannot believe. She knows it's something horrible, something she must alert the police about, and even provide help herself.<br /><br />And that's the moment when everything turns upside down. Did Anna actually see anything, or was it a hallucination from her medicine or the old movies she has seen over and over again? What is she to believe, her eyes or those who tell her what her eyes have or haven't seen? What, and who, is real? Does she have anyone or anything to fear?<br /><br />This is a taut thriller that definitely hooked me from the get-go. I had a lot of questions as I read, and wondered how Finn was going to bring everything together. While I felt like the book borrowed a lot from other thrillers and even some of the old movies Anna watched, the suspense definitely gets under your skin, and you absolutely want to fly through the book to see what the truth really is. Throughout most of the book, Anna feels like an old woman, but that's because of her condition. I had to keep reminding myself how old she really was.<br /><br />I felt like the whole story took a little too much time to play out—there were only so many times I could handle Anna's drunken binges, her not being believed by those she trusted, and her intense paranoia, which pushed everyone away. But there are some great twists here, some I didn't quite see coming and one I suspected (which disappointed me), and much like many thrillers and crime novels, the perpetrator spends far too much time explaining themselves and their motivations.<br /><br />I read a lot of thrillers so I tend to be really cynical about them. This is a good one, and I'd imagine this one is going to have many people eagerly turning the pages and staying up late because they can't get enough! <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>, or check out my list of the best books I read in 2017 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6255329421988162798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer4530350897605635296">Who's that woman in the window?<br/><br/>Dr. Anna Fox has spent the past 10 months inside her NY home. Her home is her safe place and she is too afraid to venture outside her door. <br/><br/>She entertains herself daily with the following activities:<br/>-downing bottles of Merlot and popping pills prescribed by her physician<br/>-following the lives of her neighbors through the lens of her camera<br/>-playing online chess <br/>-watching black and white films from her large collection of DVDs/mostly Hitchcock with some themes that may</span>
  <span id="freeText4530350897605635296" style="display:none">Who's that woman in the window?<br /><br />Dr. Anna Fox has spent the past 10 months inside her NY home. Her home is her safe place and she is too afraid to venture outside her door. <br /><br />She entertains herself daily with the following activities:<br />-downing bottles of Merlot and popping pills prescribed by her physician<br />-following the lives of her neighbors through the lens of her camera<br />-playing online chess <br />-watching black and white films from her large collection of DVDs/mostly Hitchcock with some themes that may later be back to haunt her<br />-talks on the phone to her ex-husband and her daughter (who he has custody of)<br /><br />This is all fine and dandy until one day while "getting to know" her new neighbors through her lens, she sees something harrowing!<br /><br />So very clever!! Yet all the clues are set out if you can "catch" them! <br /><br />Beware that the beginning is a bit confusing and takes awhile to set things in motion, but even with that I couldn't pull myself away from the story. <br /><br />Very fast read for me! Not edge of your seat, but more like the pull of a magnet. Loved this one!<br /><br />Super time reading this one with Traveling sisters! <br /><br />Thanks to Edelweiss/Wm. Morrow for my arc.</span>

<div id="review_2095580106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2095580106" />
    <a title="Dennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67496521-dennis"><img alt="Dennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597768154p2/67496521.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2095580106?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dennis" href="/user/show/67496521-dennis">Dennis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062678416" href="/book/show/34848682-the-woman-in-the-window">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=giveaways">giveaways</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=2018-pub">2018-pub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2095580106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18388278838955276705"><i>It isn't paranoia if it's really happening...</i> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>The Woman in the Window</i>
</b> is intoxicating, dark, and simply unputdownable. AJ Finn's debut novel is placed in current day, gentrified Harlem, New York City, where Dr. Anna Fox spends her day in her five-story townhouse drinking Merlot, spying on her neighbors, and mixing pills to numb her thoughts. She has theories and pseudo-storylines for her neighbors, each one being unique and different in their own way. When she is not photographing and spying</span>
  <span id="freeText18388278838955276705" style="display:none"><i>It isn't paranoia if it's really happening...</i> <br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Woman in the Window</i>
</b> is intoxicating, dark, and simply unputdownable. AJ Finn's debut novel is placed in current day, gentrified Harlem, New York City, where Dr. Anna Fox spends her day in her five-story townhouse drinking Merlot, spying on her neighbors, and mixing pills to numb her thoughts. She has theories and pseudo-storylines for her neighbors, each one being unique and different in their own way. When she is not photographing and spying on her neighbors, Anna watches famous black and white movies to pass the time and regularly checks in with her daughter and husband, who she recently has separated from. Anna suffers from agoraphobia, preventing her from leaving the confines of her house and limiting her ability to experience the real world effectively. Her hours, days, and weeks are consumed by fear and curiosity. When her new neighbors move in across the park from her house, Anna is intrigued at their anonymity. As she begins to investigate the story of her new neighbors, something horribly goes wrong. Anna witnesses something that shouldn't have happened—or did she?<br /><br />I won this ARC in a Goodreads giveaway and literally jumped out of my bed and yelled, "YESSS!!!" I immediately was drawn to the story because let's face it, spending time spying on your neighbors while drinking too much wine sounds like my Friday nights. I was curious to see how this story would develop and see what the hype was about. After getting hooked in right from the beginning, I figured out why. <b>
  <i>The Woman in the Window</i>
</b> will definitely not be for everybody. The initial pacing is moderate, to say the least. I wouldn't classify it as a slow burn however, because as the story progresses, the character development of Anna and the provided characters becomes ever more intriguing. Nothing is rushed or overlooked—everything is portrayed at exactly the right time. Why is Anna agoraphobic? What's her mental state like? How is she coping? What's going on in the outside world that she's missing? Who are all these people around her? These are just some of the questions that pulled me in while starting <b>
  <i>The Woman in the Window</i>
</b> and it kept me guessing until the end. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Woman in the Window</i>
</b> breaks away from the mold of some of the more recent in-your-face psychological thrillers that have been sprouting out more and more since the release of <i>the book that shall not be named</i>, and that's very refreshing to me. This type of psychological thriller really gets you in the mindset of Anna's psyche without throwing everything at you at once. <br /><br />As I've stated earlier, this book will not be for everyone. This thriller breaks the mold and sets a new standard—so buckle up 2018! <br /><br /><b>Thank you Goodreads and William Murrow Books for my advanced copy.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="18388278838955276705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2258569880" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2258569880" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4125660-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316269997p2/4125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2258569880?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/4125660-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/37827620-the-woman-in-the-window">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4125660-liz?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2258569880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13529196573997869905">This review is a hard one for me. I struggled with the first half of the book, only to be totally drawn in by the end. <br/><br/>The book starts offs slowly, setting the stage. Anna Fox is a child psychotherapist who suffers from agoraphobia. As she’s trapped in her house, there’s not a lot of action to begin with. But that kind of works. But a little of that goes along way and I kept waiting for something to happen to turn up the pace. <br/><br/>I definitely didn’t relate to Anna, but I also had a hard time findin</span>
  <span id="freeText13529196573997869905" style="display:none">This review is a hard one for me. I struggled with the first half of the book, only to be totally drawn in by the end. <br /><br />The book starts offs slowly, setting the stage. Anna Fox is a child psychotherapist who suffers from agoraphobia. As she’s trapped in her house, there’s not a lot of action to begin with. But that kind of works. But a little of that goes along way and I kept waiting for something to happen to turn up the pace. <br /><br />I definitely didn’t relate to Anna, but I also had a hard time finding her believable. The idea that she’d be able to consume multiple bottles of wine at one time, on top of prescription drugs and be able to speak or walk at all seemed unbelievable. I’d be comatose, not just slurring my words. However, I didn’t think of her as a stalker or a voyeur, I didn’t find her creepy that way. <br /><br />As the story goes along, I started wondering about some of the twists I assumed were coming. I correctly guessed the first big reveal well before it comes out. This book is a homage to old movies, especially Hitchcock and other film noir directors. But the movie this most reminded me of is a more recent one. I can’t name it without giving out a spoiler, which I refuse to do in a review. Flip side, I totally blew how I envisioned the ending. <br /><br />Grading this is hard. The second half of the book is much more engrossing than the first. It really took a long time to grab me. The first half of the book is barely a three, the second half is somewhere between four and 4 ½ stars. <br /><br />I listened to this and the narrator, Ann Marie Lee, did a great job. Her voice was a rainbow of nuances and emotions. But I’m wondering if this would have worked better as a book than as an audiobook. I find I like my audiobooks to be fast paced. I heard glimpses of good phrasing, something I always appreciate when I’m reading. Unfortunately, good writing is harder for me to appreciate when listening rather than reading. But that’s me, I’m definitely more visual than aural. <br />So, in the end I'm going with a 3.5 stars. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13529196573997869905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2115708364" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2115708364" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9472704-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336837712p2/9472704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2115708364?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/9472704-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062678416" href="/book/show/34848682-the-woman-in-the-window">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=mystery-thrillers">mystery-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2115708364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12496441081803709145">"I am locked in. I am locked out."<br/><br/>Anna Fox has more intricate layers than a double-decker BLT tilting towards the mayo. Ain't no toothpick strong enough to keep this one from skidding off the plate.<br/><br/>Anna exists behind the shuttered doors and windows of her four-story home in New York City. Dark and dreary are the colors that paint her reclusive world both on the exterior and on the interior. Anna suffers from agoraphobia that keeps her locked in as a prisoner of her own home and of her own mind. </span>
  <span id="freeText12496441081803709145" style="display:none">"I am locked in. I am locked out."<br /><br />Anna Fox has more intricate layers than a double-decker BLT tilting towards the mayo. Ain't no toothpick strong enough to keep this one from skidding off the plate.<br /><br />Anna exists behind the shuttered doors and windows of her four-story home in New York City. Dark and dreary are the colors that paint her reclusive world both on the exterior and on the interior. Anna suffers from agoraphobia that keeps her locked in as a prisoner of her own home and of her own mind. Those mind gremlins have taken residence and Anna sedates them with plenty of prescription drugs. She sloshes around at the bottom of a Merlot bottle like an Olympic drinker.....takin' the gold every time.<br /><br />Day by day she locks into perpetual viewing of old black and white movies including Vertigo and Rear Window. Her only interactions with the outside world are through weekly home visitations with her psychiatrist, her physical therapist, and her basement tenant, David. Anna is separated from her husband, Ed, and their young daughter, Olivia, which brings about a lonely, suffocating existence. Daily phone calls just don't seem to fill the void.<br /><br />But one bright spot comes with Anna's monitoring of her neighbor's comings and goings. She uses her Nikon camera lens to zoom in for a closer look. Such an activity brings the outside world in and gives Anna a bit of control as to when and as to how long she wishes to view their movements. She becomes particularly attached to the Russell family across the small park.<br /><br />Enter: Bizarro World in Living Color<br /><br />Anna's black and white movie world will suddenly take on techno color hues. With her up-close-and-personal camera lens, Anna witnesses something horrendous happening in the Russell's home through that window. Paralyzed with fear, Anna reports it. Let's just say that no one is buying what our Anna is selling. But, you and I the readers, we know the truth. But A.J. Finn will see to it that the truth comes in variations and all sizes......<br /><br />Wowzers! The movie rights have already been sold for this one. It's a winner. But I must honestly say that the pacing is all wrong. The beginning chapters are slow. We, the readers, circle around the storyline puffing up cushions trying to get comfy and ready. It's gonna take a while. Prepare for that. But then, it finally takes off. My other concern is the amount of pills and Merlot that Anna consumes on a daily basis. In the real world, she'd be face down, not breathing, and with carpet marks all over her face. I'll leave it there and hope the screen writers will nip and tuck.<br /><br />I encourage you to take this one out for a test drive. Cushions propped up, you might just be in for a surprise. And no Merlot required.....<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12496441081803709145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3520136099" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3520136099" />
    <a title="Dita " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26261386-dita"><img alt="Dita " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606101415p2/26261386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_2265395297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2265395297" />
    <a title="Theresa Alan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3268839-theresa-alan"><img alt="Theresa Alan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1265739602p2/3268839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2265395297?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Theresa Alan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Theresa Alan" href="/user/show/3268839-theresa-alan">Theresa Alan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35280880-the-woman-in-the-window">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2265395297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8244691662951158805">Dr. Anna Fox used to have a successful life as a mother, wife, and child psychologist, but something happened several months earlier that has given her agoraphobia. She can have her prescription medications and endless bottles of wine delivered, so she never has to leave her house. If she does want human contact, she calls her estranged husband and the daughter that lives with him. Her physical therapist and doctor come to her. There is also the online community of other people battling agorapho</span>
  <span id="freeText8244691662951158805" style="display:none">Dr. Anna Fox used to have a successful life as a mother, wife, and child psychologist, but something happened several months earlier that has given her agoraphobia. She can have her prescription medications and endless bottles of wine delivered, so she never has to leave her house. If she does want human contact, she calls her estranged husband and the daughter that lives with him. Her physical therapist and doctor come to her. There is also the online community of other people battling agoraphobia.<br /><br />Anna spies on her neighbors, camera in hand, reminiscent of Rear Window, which is the kind of movie she watches endlessly—black-and=white classics with an edge. When she sees a neighbor in trouble and the police get involved, she is not a reliable witness. People who mix prescription drugs and copious amounts of alcohol rarely are. It gets to the point she doesn’t know herself what is real—and therefore, neither do we, the readers.<br /><br />I enjoyed the suspense of this novel. <br />For more of my reviews, please visit: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.theresaalan.net/blog">http://www.theresaalan.net/blog</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8244691662951158805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_40097951'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40097951-the-silent-patient"><img alt="The Silent Patient" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1582759969l/40097951._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('K4oxAAw+WW5ob+jMG+VipOvNT3YIPgavdEnnC9Ka9MvJJ5CFcsJTJE/RLgcm+1ZTb5d8Uc9ppa/rVyhu/Wc92w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1MpZ4nQJQRR6/qkIwe1YZoz07letrctQ9GQ6AEizprI2Z/hnCvVLXl1Ab8P882yRCK7dcGr6aFBrevVlZ05vog==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7992137.A_J_Finn">About A.J. Finn</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7992137.A_J_Finn"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1513715025p3/7992137.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7992137.A_J_Finn">A.J. Finn
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
5,121
followers

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer928453708557030211">A.J. Finn, pseudonym for Daniel Mallory, has written for numerous publications, including the <i>Los Angeles Times</i>, the <i>Washington Post</i>, and the <i>Times Literary Supplement</i> (UK). A native of New York, Finn lived in England for ten years as a book editor before returning to New York City.<br/><br/></span>

</div>
</div>
